  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

        scope : 'name email',

  <span id="freeText4150015442810883339" style="display:none">Life changed for me in three days - the day my mother died, the day my dad married Candice and the day I met Kennedy Jenner. <br /><br />From the moment I saw him, I was drawn to him. Like a moth to a flame, I couldn't keep away from the irresistible heat of the fire. That knowing, confident smile...those beautiful pale blue eyes...and those dimples....simply delicious. Who could resist such a beautiful strong man?<br /><br />Hope York transformed herself from boring small town girl into a flawless beauty on the outside. But inside, she never changed. Kennedy Jenner was a successful, wealthy and jaw dropping handsome man that could have whatever he wanted, on his own terms. And he wanted Hope. But would he still want her after he saw her for who she really was, instead of what she carefully planned for everyone to see? And will his own secret past stand in his way for getting what he really wants?</span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_1885454231" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1885454231" />
    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45826136-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1523893682p2/45826136.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1885454231?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/45826136-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45826136-katerina?shelf=safe">safe</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45826136-katerina?shelf=billionaire">billionaire</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45826136-katerina?shelf=caution-themes">caution-themes</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1885454231" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12463503319500098447"><b>“I looked up to see the next guest approaching the desk for check in.  My heart skipped a beat and I stuttered “Ww<a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www..Welcome'>www..Welcome</a> to The Monet, how may I help you?”</b><br/><br/>Wow. This is insulting to womankind. We aren't dogs. We don't drool. We can see gorgeous men and the creme de la creme on the internet and in day to day life without tripping over ourselves and being rendered incapable of speech. Without having our tongues hanging out of our mouths.<br/><br/>It was a really bad regurgitation/imitation of FSOG and </span>
  <span id="freeText12463503319500098447" style="display:none"><b>“I looked up to see the next guest approaching the desk for check in.  My heart skipped a beat and I stuttered “Ww<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www..Welcome">www..Welcome</a> to The Monet, how may I help you?”</b><br /><br />Wow. This is insulting to womankind. We aren't dogs. We don't drool. We can see gorgeous men and the creme de la creme on the internet and in day to day life without tripping over ourselves and being rendered incapable of speech. Without having our tongues hanging out of our mouths.<br /><br />It was a really bad regurgitation/imitation of FSOG and Bared to You (which I love). Remember the way Gideon wanted Eva and asked her if she was sleeping with anyone? Well here we have the poor imitation. <br /><br /><b>"Are you sleeping with anyone?”  The way he asked the question was so direct but relaxed, he could have been asking for directions.<br /><br />The question caught me so off guard, I stared up at him in confusion. "Am I sleeping with someone?” <br /><br />He took one step closer, “Yes, that is the question I asked.  Would you like to know if I am sleeping with anyone before you answer?”<br /><br />I took one step back and a deep breath. “Why is it any of your business if I am sleeping with anyone Mr. Jenner?”<br /></b><br /><br />This had really crap writing. With the obvious trope of a heroine being a prude vs the sexually confident alpha man. He stops whatever fuck-buddy arrangement he has. They are lusty. <br />He wipes her down intimately afterwards. She wears his big shirt. She has the typical bitchy step mom, shes annoying, she's secretly insecure, etc etc. <br /><br />But this heroine has no brains. She agrees to literally anything he says. Stay with me? Okay. Kiss me? Okay. Strip for me? Okay Poop on me? Okay. Let me buy you lots of shit because I have money and want to lavish you? Okay but I have good clothes. Let me? Okay, you are the controller of my fate and destiny. <br /><br />What's worse is that she doesn't google him. In this day and age it isn't f*cking invasive. A smart woman would, but noo, she wants to learn about it from him. Eventually she does...after he temporarily kicks her to the curb. His little sad past is revealed...<br /><b> <br />“The organization was founded in honor of Kelly Preston, Mr. Jenner’s high school sweetheart.  Ms. Preston disappeared seven years ago, at the age of 15 while walking to a friend’s home.”</b><br /><br />He's 32 now. How is this 7 years ago? Unless the article she's reading is old. Because he couldn't have been 25 to a 15 year old girl. Plus it's mentioned he was 15. I didn't appreciate the inconsistencies. <br /><br />The grammar was atrocious. I'm willing to forgive the author because I've read books of hers before, and this was really, really, really bad. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12463503319500098447" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15877073665351708114"> There were things about this book I really liked:<br/>-the premise is irresistible to me.. Damaged rich hot guy, sweet girl beautiful on the inside and not knowing how pretty she is on the inside.. Over done and predictable, I know, but I'm a sucker..<br/>What I didn't like:<br/>-the character development was awful and inconsistent. Who they were presented as and who they were throughout the book were completely different. And I don't mean in a 'growing, and maturing and evolving as a person' kind of way.. Ju</span>
  <span id="freeText15877073665351708114" style="display:none"> There were things about this book I really liked:<br />-the premise is irresistible to me.. Damaged rich hot guy, sweet girl beautiful on the inside and not knowing how pretty she is on the inside.. Over done and predictable, I know, but I'm a sucker..<br />What I didn't like:<br />-the character development was awful and inconsistent. Who they were presented as and who they were throughout the book were completely different. And I don't mean in a 'growing, and maturing and evolving as a person' kind of way.. Just in an inconsistent disjointed kind of way. It was distracting and annoying. <br />-I didn't really feel the spark or the driving force of any of the characters (partially because of the lack of depth mentioned earlier). It's hard to get in to those books where you're sort of left questioning what the draw is- why is he so drawn to her? Why is everyone so drawn to her? Why is she so caught up in him? Suddenly her happiness depends on whether he calls her etc.. And it's kind of pathetic and immature. Over all I enjoyed it as a quick easy read, but if you like a story that you get caught up in, and really FEEL the characters and connections etc, then this might not be for you.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessy (Jessy&#39;s Book Club)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessy (Jessy&#39;s Book Club)" href="/user/show/13319152-jessy-jessy-s-book-club">Jessy (Jessy&#39;s Book Club)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13319152-jessy-jessy-s-book-club?shelf=erotic-romance">erotic-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13319152-jessy-jessy-s-book-club?shelf=possessive-controlling-men">possessive-controlling-men</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13319152-jessy-jessy-s-book-club?shelf=alpha-male">alpha-male</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13319152-jessy-jessy-s-book-club?shelf=like-fifty-shades">like-fifty-shades</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer526554437" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15250881882041285658">[Read more reviews at <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://jessysbookclub.wordpress.com/'>http://jessysbookclub.wordpress.com/</a>]<br/><br/>I was excited to start this one. It sounded very Fifty Shades of Grey to me and the whole idea of ‘Sex, secrets and dominance, with a little love story in between’ was one I couldn’t resist.<br/><br/>Let’s start with a bit of a synopsis. Hope has not always been considered pretty. She loses some pounds, styles up and moves from her small town to start a new job at one of the plushiest Hotels in New York. On her first day of training she meets Kenn</span>
  <span id="freeText15250881882041285658" style="display:none">[Read more reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://jessysbookclub.wordpress.com/">http://jessysbookclub.wordpress.com/</a>]<br /><br />I was excited to start this one. It sounded very Fifty Shades of Grey to me and the whole idea of ‘Sex, secrets and dominance, with a little love story in between’ was one I couldn’t resist.<br /><br />Let’s start with a bit of a synopsis. Hope has not always been considered pretty. She loses some pounds, styles up and moves from her small town to start a new job at one of the plushiest Hotels in New York. On her first day of training she meets Kennedy Jenner. (I’ve actually never considered the name Kennedy sexy but this one changed my mind ;) ) Anyway, it’s lust at first sight and so it begins.<br /><br />Some conversations felt stilted to me and there were some grammatical errors. Also the scenes told in Hope’s POV made me feel like I was reading somebody’s journal. I didn’t “live” it with her which is what normally happens when I read 1st person POVs.<br /><br />That aside the steamy scenes were exactly that, steamy! Kennedy is Alpha, controlling, possessive, sweet…so yes, I liked him. Hope is very insecure and usually I prefer strong heroines but I understood her insecurity and it didn’t put me off as it normally would. In fact that’s why Kennedy felt drawn to her, gorgeous but sweet, almost innocently so.<br /><br />There’s nothing surprisingly new about the storyline; tortured hero + tortured heroine = great sex. :) That being said, I liked the book. The ending was so beautiful! I was surprised there was no cliffhanger which probably means this is a stand alone. Surprising isn’t it? I’m getting used to Erotic Romance coming in trilogies.<br /><br />I’ll end by saying this, if you like erotic romance with billionaires who meet girl next door types and fall totally and hopelessly in love while having steamy steamy sex in the process then you should give this one a go.<br /><br />3 stars.</span>

          </span>

    <a title="Jillian (NetGalley Addict)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9844373-jillian-netgalley-addict"><img alt="Jillian (NetGalley Addict)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1412272746p2/9844373.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/525781444?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jillian (NetGalley Addict)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jillian (NetGalley Addict)" href="/user/show/9844373-jillian-netgalley-addict">Jillian (NetGalley Addict)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17233783-first-thing-i-see">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer525781444" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14686573463918707576">I received a copy of this book in exchange for my honest review.<br/><br/>Hope has recently moved to New York and started her dream job as an event planner at a five start hotel. On her first day of training she meets Kennedy Jenner, a wealthy business man who is staying at the hotel. They start an intense relationship complicated by her insecurities, his past demons and the thousand miles in between Chicago and New York. I was a little bit annoyed at the female main character when the book first started;</span>
  <span id="freeText14686573463918707576" style="display:none">I received a copy of this book in exchange for my honest review.<br /><br />Hope has recently moved to New York and started her dream job as an event planner at a five start hotel. On her first day of training she meets Kennedy Jenner, a wealthy business man who is staying at the hotel. They start an intense relationship complicated by her insecurities, his past demons and the thousand miles in between Chicago and New York. I was a little bit annoyed at the female main character when the book first started; she seemed weak and self conscious. It took me awhile to warm up to Hope and once I got the background story I respected her a lot more. Kennedy was a rich, gorgeous man with a damaged past and an overprotective streak that made me want to slap him at times. The problems that the two of them had were realistic and not over the top. The cheerleader best friend was a good influence on Hope with her encouragement and understanding. Hopes dad was endearing and I felt bad for him because the step-mom was a raging bitch with a side helping of slut. The Jenner family was supportive of Kennedy and his niece was beyond adorable. The love scenes were scorching hot and I really liked that their whole relationship was not based on sex. The couple seemed to share a genuine connection that kept them together when other people would have given up. I liked the book, but I really wish it had an epilogue.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14686573463918707576" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_537888929" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/537888929" />
    <a title="Lisa Borbeck" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10094424-lisa-borbeck"><img alt="Lisa Borbeck" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1357179043p2/10094424.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/537888929?book_show_action=true">Feb 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa Borbeck" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa Borbeck" href="/user/show/10094424-lisa-borbeck">Lisa Borbeck</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer537888929" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16576019082591148630">This book is Fifty Shades of Grey meets Cinderella. Please, don’t misunderstand me. This isn’t just an x-rated fairy tale and Kennedy Jenner is no Prince Charming. Hope York moves from Chicago to New York to not only distance herself from her mean as a junk yard dog Step-Mother Candace, but to essentially change who she is. Years of verbal abuse at the hands of Candace has convinced Hope that she is ugly and worthless so she decides to transform herself both inside and out. On her very first day</span>
  <span id="freeText16576019082591148630" style="display:none">This book is Fifty Shades of Grey meets Cinderella. Please, don’t misunderstand me. This isn’t just an x-rated fairy tale and Kennedy Jenner is no Prince Charming. Hope York moves from Chicago to New York to not only distance herself from her mean as a junk yard dog Step-Mother Candace, but to essentially change who she is. Years of verbal abuse at the hands of Candace has convinced Hope that she is ugly and worthless so she decides to transform herself both inside and out. On her very first day as an Event Planner at a 5 star hotel, she meets Kennedy, millionaire playboy and is swept away by his charm and looks. Kennedy on the other hand has never met anyone like Hope before and he makes it his life mission to get to know Hope better. Not used to getting his way, it just adds to his desire for her. This cat and mouse game does not go on for too long which actually surprised me, I thought the dance would be longer. As the two learn about each other, we slowly learn about each’s back story and peel back the layers to see just how messed up these two individuals truly are.<br />I seriously enjoyed the hell out of this story. I didn’t realize that sometimes you just don’t want to wait till the end of the book before a couple gets together. At times I felt that Hope was a bit tstl and Kennedy was an overbearing bossy fuck but those times were few and far between and didn’t piss me off enough for me to want to stop reading. There was just enough sex to make this an erotic book but not so much that made me feel like I was reading a porno. I don’t understand why it seems that every other male lead out there is a multi million dollar playboy who was just waiting for the right girl to make him want to stop sticking it in everything that moved and settle down but it worked for this story. I give it 4.5 feathers and would like to see this author perhaps write a follow up story with Shauna and Garret.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16576019082591148630" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_601736474" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/601736474" />
    <a title="Michelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13126896-michelle"><img alt="Michelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1505605297p2/13126896.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/601736474?book_show_action=true">Apr 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle" href="/user/show/13126896-michelle">Michelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13126896-michelle?shelf=01-signed">01-signed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer601736474" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13641240394979119592">A great read, little drama and little angst. Made a relaxing read for a Sunday after finishing a few intense reads. My first experience with Vi Keeland was with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17458478.Belong_To_You' title='Belong To You by Vi Keeland' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1362354451s/17458478.jpg' alt='Belong To You by Vi Keeland' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a>, and I loved it. First Thing I See was no different. I fell into the ease of the story quickly.<br/><br/><br/>Hope York has left her home in Oregon for New York. Leaving behind an image of herself that had very little self-confidence due to harsh words from her step-mother, she is starting over in a new place where she can be the woman she wants t</span>
  <span id="freeText13641240394979119592" style="display:none">A great read, little drama and little angst. Made a relaxing read for a Sunday after finishing a few intense reads. My first experience with Vi Keeland was with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17458478.Belong_To_You" title="Belong To You by Vi Keeland" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1362354451s/17458478.jpg" alt="Belong To You by Vi Keeland" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a>, and I loved it. First Thing I See was no different. I fell into the ease of the story quickly.<br><br><br>Hope York has left her home in Oregon for New York. Leaving behind an image of herself that had very little self-confidence due to harsh words from her step-mother, she is starting over in a new place where she can be the woman she wants to be. After getting hired at The Monet, a five-star hotel as the event planner she is learning the ropes. She is not prepared with she comes face to face with a man that has her knees weak the minute she spots blue eyes and dimples. One encounter may just change her entire life. <br><br>But even as Hope strives to be the version of herself that everyone else sees, she still has some struggles to beat that voice out of her head that she is not good enough. She is the girl who everyone notices, but the girl who barely notices herself. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380419323i/831165.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Kennedy Jenner is a successful business man. One look at Hope and he knows he must have her. Even if it is one time get her out of his thoughts. But he is consumed by her and slowly he starts alter his lifestyle - giving into a relationship with a woman, rather than just an arrangement. Kennedy seems perfect; rich, kind, sweet, sexy, protective and hot. But his past is something that has made him distant. A need to protect Hope - a need that she doesn't understand at first. A painful event that causes a man to hold himself guilty for, a incident that a boy could not prevent or control. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380419323i/831166.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This was a very sweet romantic story of two lives that intersect and connect. It was a safe read for me, but it is the story that we all love. These are still my guilty pleasure reads. I am glad that I was pointed into Vi's direction and will no doubt enjoy her future books - especially if she keeps delivering hot blue eyed guys with dimples.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/571484.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="13641240394979119592" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/559194729?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cocktails and Books" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cocktails and Books" href="/user/show/3769521-cocktails-and-books">Cocktails and Books</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3769521-cocktails-and-books?shelf=cnb-reviewers">cnb-reviewers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer559194729" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8389849870786030413">A perfect blend of romance, sex and reality, this book was beautiful, sweet, and real. Hope lands her dream job in a plush New York hotel. It’s here, on her first day, that she runs in to Kennedy, a wealthy man who knows exactly what he wants. When they meet, there’s an instant attraction that can be felt as you read the words on the page, and their whirlwind romance begins.<br/><br/>The characters that the author created for this story shared a chemistry that felt real. Hope was insecure, sweet and ambit</span>
  <span id="freeText8389849870786030413" style="display:none">A perfect blend of romance, sex and reality, this book was beautiful, sweet, and real. Hope lands her dream job in a plush New York hotel. It’s here, on her first day, that she runs in to Kennedy, a wealthy man who knows exactly what he wants. When they meet, there’s an instant attraction that can be felt as you read the words on the page, and their whirlwind romance begins.<br /><br />The characters that the author created for this story shared a chemistry that felt real. Hope was insecure, sweet and ambitious, and those insecurities made it really easy for me to relate to her feelings. Kennedy is the epitome of an Alpha male. Strong, sexy, dominant, and with a “broken” past, he has poured so much of himself into his work, creating situations where he sees something he wants and he takes it. When the two of them meet, their worlds are turned upside down and an intense relationship develops between the two of them. Their moments of intimacy are erotic and tastefully written; making their relationship all the more beautiful, and their romance, while flawed like most, is just perfect.<br /><br />If you’re looking for a Fifty Shades type of dominance (minus the childish drama), you’ll thoroughly enjoy First Thing I See.<br /><br />Reviewed by Marie for Cocktails and Books</span>
  <a data-text-id="8389849870786030413" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14583257479037959036">This book was ok for me. I've read books by this author that I've really enjoyed, but this one just fell flat. First of all, we only read of two physical encounters between Kennedy and Hope before they have sex. The author says that they have been texting and calling each other every day, but there is no written dialogue to give us a sense of their attraction to each other. Therefore, I could not really feel their chemistry for each other. A few times, I felt like there was an error of which nam</span>
  <span id="freeText14583257479037959036" style="display:none">This book was ok for me. I've read books by this author that I've really enjoyed, but this one just fell flat. First of all, we only read of two physical encounters between Kennedy and Hope before they have sex. The author says that they have been texting and calling each other every day, but there is no written dialogue to give us a sense of their attraction to each other. Therefore, I could not really feel their chemistry for each other. A few times, I felt like there was an error of which name they would place (purely editing). There was no closure about Mikayla, which was odd because she showed up everywhere. There was no closure with Candace (I would have loved to have read a crazy confrontation or cat fight involving her). And the end of the book came to an abrupt stop. So it was kind of weird and took me a moment to realize that was it. There were some really nicely written parts but overall, the book itself needed to have a little bit more depth and closure.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14583257479037959036" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('nIAYRZMhk6B0R6TUfWY1sjNWhEyR/KZslpuzifE5igae0SaSLccMv8syL1G138fhD9AnTZOtuXgnMWhU3Nwd9Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('bvXP6CTxvJpBvY8J9cC6rImOEYoVH8tNgE0qQZ0hD5dspPE/mhcjhf7IBIw9eUj/tQiyixdO1Fkx5/GcsMSYZA==')})
  }

        script.src = load[i];
        first.parentNode.insertBefore(script, first);
      }
    }
  if (w.attachEvent) {
    w.attachEvent('onload', go);
  } else {
    w.addEventListener('load', go, false);
  }
}(window, document,
    ['//assets.pinterest.com/js/pinit.js',
     '//apis.google.com/js/plusone.js'
    ]
  ));

//]]>
</script>

      </div>

    </div>
